| 1:25:34| We went over this in agenda review.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5134)|
| 1:25:36| This request came from a city council member to look at signage standards for the institutional district.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5136)|
| 1:25:44| The signage standards are dictated by the zone classification and by the classification of the highway on which the property is located.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5144)|
| 1:25:55| There was concern, I believe, that institutional zones surrounded by residential districts would have large signs.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5155)|
| 1:26:04| In the review that staff did, and you've got some of that, most of the properties, 16 properties,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5164)|
| 1:26:11| are zoned institutional with frontage on a federally designated highway,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5171)|
| 1:26:16| meaning they could have a sign of approximately 165 square feet or 20 feet in height.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5176)|
| 1:26:25| All of those except one is a state, county, or city facility and not subject to the city zoning ordinance.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5185)|
| 1:26:34| One of them is owned by the Industrial Development Board, and I'm not sure what that entity is.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5194)|
| 1:26:41| I don't know.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5201)|
| 1:26:42| I think we have control over it, but they're at Paper Mill and I-640.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5202)|
| 1:26:49| Even though there's nearby residential, it's multifamily and a sign of that size would be appropriate.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5209)|
| 1:26:56| I looked further, and Karen has some of them up.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5216)|
| 1:26:59| The institutional zones that are not on a federally designated highway are adjacent to residential are schools.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5219)|

| 1:28:34| I'm not sure I am.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5314)|
| 1:28:35| But anyway, Scenic Knoxville does not support the planning staff's recommendation| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5315)|
| 1:28:40| that no revisions be made to the signed standards for properties zoned institutional.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5320)|
| 1:28:46| According to planning staff, and as stated in your agenda packet,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5326)|
| 1:28:50| when designating properties for institutional zoning on the new zoning map,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5330)|
| 1:28:56| the minimum acreage that was used as a guide, not a standard,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5336)|
| 1:29:01| but a guide for these designations was five acres, as Mr. Green just said.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5341)|
| 1:29:08| Properties zoned institutional are described, again from your packet,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5348)|
| 1:29:13| as large, complex, and a campus-like setting.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5353)|
| 1:29:17| Your packet also states that planning staff has since conducted research| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5357)|
| 1:29:21| using the properties that have been zoned institutional, and Mr. Green just reviewed that.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5361)|
| 1:29:28| And so I'm going to say, and the conclusion was that most of these properties would be eligible| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5368)|
| 1:29:34| for a 10-foot tall, 100-square foot sign.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5374)|
| 1:29:39| And staff concluded, and I quote,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5379)|
| 1:29:42| this sign size is appropriate for properties with a minimum size of five acres,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5382)|
| 1:29:48| which is the threshold for schools and churches to be designated institutional.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5388)|
| 1:29:54| There are several problems with this conclusion.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5394)|
| 1:29:56| First of all, Article 8 of the new zoning code introduces the institutional district in Section 8.2.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5396)|
| 1:30:05| In Section 8.2a, the purpose statement states that,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5405)|
| 1:30:09| in addition to medical centers and schools,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5409)|
| 1:30:12| this designation can be used for professional offices or business uses| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5412)|
| 1:30:17| that are compatible with the character of the district.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5417)|
| 1:30:21| Currently, properties zoned office in the office zone are allowed a maximum of a six-foot monument sign.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5421)|
| 1:30:29| According to the arguments made here,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5429)|
| 1:30:32| offices located adjacent to a residential district that are zoned institutional| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5432)|
| 1:30:40| would likely be allowed a 10-foot, 100-square foot detached sign.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5440)|
| 1:30:47| It does not make sense that office space located within a residential district| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5447)|
| 1:30:52| or adjacent or surrounded by a residential district| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5452)|
| 1:30:56| is allowed larger signage than office space located in an office zone.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5456)|
| 1:31:02| More importantly, in Table 8.2 of the ordinance,| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5462)|
| 1:31:06| and I know you can't read this, but I am going to pass on a copy of my remarks.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5466)|
| 1:31:11| The minimum lot area is specified as 20,000 square feet in Table 8.2, or less than half an acre.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=5471)|

| 1:55:14| general commercial, highway commercial, CR, IRD, IG for the planned zones.| [source video](https://archive.org/details/planningr399191114part2?start=6914)|
